## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and/or external driving terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear damping with restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically driven damped oscillator)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum-like restoring force)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (saturating restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb-damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2 + c2)**(-0.5) (friction-like damping approximation)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power restoring terms (x²) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection
- Terms like x²*v or v³ → amplitude-dependent damping (self-sustained oscillations, limit cycles)
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- sin(x) restoring force → pendulum-type large-angle oscillations with bounded potential
- Product of x and trigonometric function of t → parametric excitation / Mathieu-type instability
- Absence of explicit t dependence → autonomous system, energy-based analysis applicable
- Cubic x term with opposite sign to linear x term → double-well (Duffing) potential with bistability
- Ratio of velocity terms to position terms → quality factor / damping ratio characterization

**GT:** `-0.0458938827292319*v**3 - 1.28311219603499*x**3 - 0.729560991204844*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333`

The GT has three terms:
1. A `v**3` term
2. An `x**3` term
3. An `|v|^(1/3)` term

The key challenge is the `|v|^(1/3)` term. None of the candidate formulas contain `Abs(v)**c` with a fractional power. Let me check what structures are available.

Most candidates have structures like:
- `c*x`, `c*x**2`, `c*x**3`, `c*x**5`
- `c*v`, `c*v**3`, `c*v**2*x`, `c*v*x`, `c*v*x**2`
- `c*v*Abs(v)` (candidates 6, 43)
- Various time-dependent terms: `cos(...)`, `exp(sin(...))`, etc.

For time-dependent terms, I can set their coefficients to 0 to eliminate them. So the question is whether the remaining terms can produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

**No candidate has `|v|^(1/3)`** or any term that could produce it. Let me verify:

- `v*Abs(v)` = `|v|*v` = `sign(v)*v**2`, which is an odd function of v with power 2, not 1/3.
- `v**3` is odd with power 3.
- `v` is odd with power 1.
- `v**2*x` mixes v and x.

The term `Abs(v)**0.333...` is an **even** function of v. None of the candidate terms that are even in v (like `v**2*x`) can match `|v|^(1/3)` because they have different functional forms.

Let me double-check: Could `exp(c*sin(...))` somehow produce `|v|^(1/3)`? No, because these are functions of `t`, not `v`.

Could `exp(c*x)` produce it? No, it's a function of `x`, not `v`.

Could any combination of the available terms produce `|v|^(1/3)`? The available v-dependent terms are polynomial in v (like v, v**2*x, v**3, v*|v|, v*x, v*x**2). No finite combination of these polynomial terms can equal `|v|^(1/3)`, which is a fractional power with fundamentally different behavior (infinite derivative at v=0, different growth rate, etc.).

Let me also check: is `v*Abs(v)` equivalent to `sign(v)*v**2`? Yes. Could this somehow help? No, because `|v|^(1/3)` is even in v while `v*Abs(v)` is odd.

None of the candidates contain a term that could reproduce the `|v|^(1/3)` behavior. The GT fundamentally requires a fractional power of `|v|`, and no candidate provides such a term or any combination of terms that could produce it.

Even if we consider that `|v|^(1/3)` might be approximated, we need **exact** mathematical equivalence, not approximation.

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.0459*v³ - 1.283*x³ - 0.7296*|v|^(1/3)`

The GT depends only on `x` and `v` (not `t`), and contains three terms: `v³`, `x³`, and `|v|^(1/3)`.

**Key observations:**
- GT has no `t` dependence, so any `t`-dependent terms must be eliminable (set to zero).
- GT has no `x`, `x²`, `v`, `v²x`, `vx`, `x⁵`, etc. terms.
- GT requires `|v|^(1/3)`, which is a very specific basis function.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce `|v|^(1/3)`:

**None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or `Abs(v)^(1/3)`.** Let me look more carefully...

The candidates contain terms like: `v`, `v³`, `v²x`, `v*x²`, `v*|v|` (= |v|*v which is sign(v)*v²), `cos(...)`, `exp(...)`, `x`, `x²`, `x³`, `x⁵`, etc.

The term `|v|^(1/3)` is a fractional power of an absolute value. None of the standard basis functions in any candidate (polynomials in v, x, t; trigonometric; exponential) can produce `|v|^(1/3)`.

Let me verify: Can any combination of the available terms equal `|v|^(1/3)`? No — `|v|^(1/3)` is not a polynomial, not an exponential, not trigonometric. It's a fundamentally different basis function. By the linear independence of these function classes, no finite combination of polynomials, exponentials, and trigonometric functions can equal `|v|^(1/3)` for all values of `v`.

Even `v*Abs(v)` (in Candidates 6, 43) gives `sign(v)*v²`, which is not `|v|^(1/3)`.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because the essential `|v|^(1/3)` term cannot be reproduced by any of the available basis functions.

- Candidates 1-50: All use combinations of `x`, `x²`, `x³`, `x⁵`, `v`, `v³`, `v²x`, `vx`, `vx²`, `v*|v|`, `cos(...)`, `sin(...)`, `exp(...)`, `log(...)` — none of which can produce `|v|^(1/3)`.
